<span id="freeTextContainer15366098614977161171"><b>Book recommended for die-hard YA somewhat-realistic Romance fans.</b><br/>Blurb:<br/>17 year old Kari was taken advantage of a year ago, since then she's been living life on a knifes edge. Kari attends college (as the youngest in her class) and takes up a job as a tattoo artist in a tattoo and piercing salon called 'The Prick'. After working there for a while she meets her boss's son, Neil. Neil is hot, rides a motorbike and likes dancing... Neil makes her believe there are good guys after all.<br/><br/>Why is it somew</span>
  <span id="freeText15366098614977161171" style="display:none"><b>Book recommended for die-hard YA somewhat-realistic Romance fans.</b><br />Blurb:<br />17 year old Kari was taken advantage of a year ago, since then she's been living life on a knifes edge. Kari attends college (as the youngest in her class) and takes up a job as a tattoo artist in a tattoo and piercing salon called 'The Prick'. After working there for a while she meets her boss's son, Neil. Neil is hot, rides a motorbike and likes dancing... Neil makes her believe there are good guys after all.<br /><br />Why is it somewhat-realistic? Well for a start she's a 17 year old tattoo artist. Neil is a fan of dance. Neil is 26, and this doesn't seem a problem. Things just seemed to come out of the blue and were a little far fetched at times. There was the confusing first chapter, which was probably not needed. And the book switched from a YA romantic humour to an angsty teen book every so often. I also think it should have a more appropriate title and cover, (the saucy cover does not fit a YA book).<br /><br />Why I liked it? There were some silly LOL moments for me, there was fun and a gentle romance. The supporting characters were fun, Kari was also, but Neil was a little bit boring for me. I really don't think it's for everyone. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Never make eye contact with a stranger when you're having a churro.”<br />“What?” I scrunch my face at Nalini who's taken it upon herself to educate me in the ways for the world.<br />“And it applies to a banana as well.”<br /><br />“Boys are like candy.” she suddenly says.<br />I grin “Really, Mom? That's your advice? Boys are like candy. What's that? Forrest Gump on teens?”</i>
</b><br /><br /><br />Writing style: 7/10<br />Humour: 7/10<br />Characters: 6/10<br />Romance: 8/10<br />Ending: 6/10<br /><br />My star ratings:<br />1* Complete trash<br />2* Waste of time really, but I carried on for some reason<br />3* Half decent, usually down to personal preferences<br />4* Could read this again, only a little thing is missing, maybe more humour or romance etc...<br />5* Would read this again and again, unique story, adore this author</span>

Now Eddie seems to be a bit of a movie star at her school, always giving presentations and talk sessions to young kids.   <span id="freeText15332957020740861771" style="display:none">Kari is a young 16 year old schoolgirl who likes to keep herself to herself.<br /><br />Whilst she’s out walking home from school she meet the elusive Eddie. Now Eddie seems to be a bit of a movie star at her school, always giving presentations and talk sessions to young kids. He comes off as a respectable elder, little do we know he is a serious SLEAZEBALL<br /><br />We see Eddie’s actions as he seduces young Kari and eventually sleeps with this young “Virgin”, bear in mind he’s like 18-19.<br /><br />Kari is on top of the world right now, that is until Eddie drops a bombshell…….He video tapped the whole thing!<br /><br />We are then fast forwarded 2 years in the future and we learn just how much of a sleazeball Eddie actually is.<br /><br />He demands money from Kari to keep his mouth shut.<br /><br />This ghost of her past is still hanging on tight and will not let her go no matter what.<br /><br />In swoops her saving grace “Neil Mars” As a reader I fell in love this character immediately! I mean how Rucy describes Neil in the book is HOT and you’ll want him to swoop you off your feet and rescue you!<br /><br />The sexual tension between Neil &amp; Kari throughout this book is awesome, I freaking loved it.<br /><br />As you can imagine though Kari tries her best to elude Neil in every way.<br /><br />She’s closed herself off from men, but for some reason Neil has gotten through her barriers, and it scares her.<br /><br />Kari is a broken, fragile girl who needs to be loved the way a young girl should be loved, and there’s no one better then Mr Neil Mars.<br /><br />Rucy Ban’s writing was packed full of emotions &amp; flirtatious banter between the young love couple.<br /><br />This book is Sexy, fun and passionate.<br /><br />I honestly can’t wait to read the second installment “Wear You Down”, which is expected to be released November 2013</span>

        <a title="Jesey ~ Schmexy GIrl~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesey ~ Schmexy GIrl~" href="/user/show/19431942-jesey-schmexy-girl">Jesey ~ Schmexy GIrl~</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1079420208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8194631218504787292">When young Kari first sees Neil, she has no idea who he is. She spots him across the street from the tattoo shop she has started working at and he is making out with some girl in blue high heels. Kari finds herself staring and quickly nicknames him the “Mad Kisser”. She comes to find out that he is her boss’ son but little does she know that he will turn her world upside down.<br/><br/> <br/><br/>Neil is instantly attracted to Kari and asks her out after she finishes giving him a tattoo. Kari views herself as broke</span>
  <span id="freeText8194631218504787292" style="display:none">When young Kari first sees Neil, she has no idea who he is. She spots him across the street from the tattoo shop she has started working at and he is making out with some girl in blue high heels. Kari finds herself staring and quickly nicknames him the “Mad Kisser”. She comes to find out that he is her boss’ son but little does she know that he will turn her world upside down.<br /><br /> <br /><br />Neil is instantly attracted to Kari and asks her out after she finishes giving him a tattoo. Kari views herself as broken and troubled and feels like her life is ruined because of a foolish mistake that now haunts her. She tells Neil that she does not date. This does not deter Neil at all. He is sweet, kind, generous, and oddly intuitive about Kari.<br /><br /><br /><br /> <br /><br />“This guy. This. Guy. He’s going to break my heart.”<br /><br /> <br /><br /> <br /><br />As their relationship blooms Kari invites Neil to meet her mom. It is this night she learns a secret about him and when we also learn that he is 26…this threw me off a little because Kari is only 17. I know that age is only a number but he is much older, has a fabulous career, and is caring for his sick mother. It seems like so much for this supposedly broken girl to handle. Over the course of what is about a week these two fall madly in love with each other, change who they are, and one is willing to give up everything for the other.<br /><br />The story was sweet and I enjoyed reading it. Personally I couldn’t get past the whole age thing for some reason. I did like that they story wrapped up at the end so we know what happens for them.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer666516535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10600948831101044860">A fun summer book with a (mostly) happy ending. What I liked most is the main character’s voice. Kari is the ultimate teenager who is mature at certain times and childlike and naïve at others. She goes from being self-conscious and even self-centered to developing awareness of others and being more equipped to solve problems, her own and those of other people. The present tense that the author uses works great for this character, allowing for events to unfold in real time without too many chance</span>
  <span id="freeText10600948831101044860" style="display:none">A fun summer book with a (mostly) happy ending. What I liked most is the main character’s voice. Kari is the ultimate teenager who is mature at certain times and childlike and naïve at others. She goes from being self-conscious and even self-centered to developing awareness of others and being more equipped to solve problems, her own and those of other people. The present tense that the author uses works great for this character, allowing for events to unfold in real time without too many chances for reflection and analysis. Kari’s life is too full and too busy to reflect on any single event for too long, and the choice of the present tense narrative emphasizes that trait of her character.<br /><br />I enjoyed the author’s sense of humor, mostly portrayed through Kari’s thoughts and comments. The romance aspect felt very YA, just like the main character herself: overwhelming, all-encompassing, and thrilling for Kari.<br /><br />Romance aside, Kari is faced with serious (and realistic) problems that teens her age and younger could face in today’s technology-centered world, but she manages to overcome them with her own determination, with help from her friends, and with a number of lucky coincidences. <br /><br />If you are looking for a dark, deep, tragic YA story, this book is not for you. However, if you want to spend some time with a group of quirky characters and watch them overcome life’s various challenges, then pick up this novel. It’s a quick read and a great escape from everyday life.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10600948831101044860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer693423744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5810909656495865414">I made in about 75 pages into this and even though I was more than halfway done, I could not read another page of Kari's ridiculous dialogue. I know she's 17, but she's one of the most immature characters I've ever come across. So. Many. Exclamation. Points!!!! Interjections such as: "Christ!" and my personal least facorite, "JHEEZUS!" No...I just can't anymore.<br/><br/>And of course there's the insta-lust between Kari and the guy, Neil. He calls her, for no reason, Angel. ANGEL. It came across as very c</span>
  <span id="freeText5810909656495865414" style="display:none">I made in about 75 pages into this and even though I was more than halfway done, I could not read another page of Kari's ridiculous dialogue. I know she's 17, but she's one of the most immature characters I've ever come across. So. Many. Exclamation. Points!!!! Interjections such as: "Christ!" and my personal least facorite, "JHEEZUS!" No...I just can't anymore.<br /><br />And of course there's the insta-lust between Kari and the guy, Neil. He calls her, for no reason, Angel. ANGEL. It came across as very corny to me. <br /><br />If there were a sex tape floating around that contained me, you can damn well BET that I would not be paying blackmail money to the dude to released it! She gives some excuses as to why in the beginning, but they don't make much sense. My first thought? If someone released a sex tape where the girl was 16 years old, isn't that CHILD PORNOGRAPHY? I dunno. Maybe all reasoning has gone out the window here.<br /><br />To make a long story short, this is not a good addition to the new adult genre at all. Stay away.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer599490656" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11868342048129563133">**I was given an ARC in exchange for an honest review**<br/><br/>For a debut novel, Rucy Ban did a fantastic job of writing this book. She created a great cast of characters that complimented each other & dialogue that flowed. Its packed with emotion, ranging from shock (quite a few WTF moments)to fear, to excitement and of course love. <br/><br/>Kari had a pretty bad experience the first time she fell in love with a boy & it still follows her... Literally. <br/>She tries to move on with her life but it proves to be dif</span>
  <span id="freeText11868342048129563133" style="display:none">**I was given an ARC in exchange for an honest review**<br /><br />For a debut novel, Rucy Ban did a fantastic job of writing this book. She created a great cast of characters that complimented each other &amp; dialogue that flowed. Its packed with emotion, ranging from shock (quite a few WTF moments)to fear, to excitement and of course love. <br /><br />Kari had a pretty bad experience the first time she fell in love with a boy &amp; it still follows her... Literally. <br />She tries to move on with her life but it proves to be difficult when her past is blackmailing her. <br /><br />Then she meets Neil - a sexy, muscular guy who happens to be the son of her new boss. <br /><br />At first things start out slow, Kari is scared that Neil will discover her secret &amp; leave, while Neil is afraid to let anyone know why he came back to town. <br /><br />This was a sweet read with lots of quirky banter, angst &amp; a touch of smexy.<br /><br />**Highly Recommended**</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lNobsHlmkgaDgtcHAph86HGmkAlJ1ODLT/b6MkGqkGCFyVaVWCFKD0mQHZFpt83tAkR6JmOLdefGjXSEGqeW8g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('l8DkIIDZJvt5ThDu3xp325tjfPkDFHbMpRswjlKYeD2G06kFoZ7+8rNc2ni0Ncbe6IGW1ilL4+AsYL44CZV+rw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
